Reading Q&A

How to Study the Northeast Problem (3) 169

Yesterday and the day before, the problem was raised, and a little criticism was added to Mr. Fang's viewpoint. Today, we will further study the method, but first, we should still discuss the principles. Tomorrow, we will apply the principles to the dissection of the problem. Editor

Before proposing how to study the Northeast problem, we want to especially ask readers to pay attention to why we accept the review of this problem; why not ask you to read books, but instead talk about this old account that the Chinese people are familiar with? We have already briefly mentioned the reason in the front, and now we want to repeat it, just hoping to arouse those of you who are learning social sciences to apply the theories you have learned to practical problems after pondering and contemplating. Here, we are just acting as an example, suggesting some methods of application. Naturally, we cannot analyze in more detail, nor can we say that there are no shortcomings. This is due to the limitations of the length and the interests of this column. At the same time, we are not writing articles here, discussing "national affairs," expressing great opinions. We are just taking the attitude of a "teacher"—if it is not too presumptuous—to lead "students"—these two words are not very appropriate either, please readers do not laugh at our arrogance—to practice. However, although it is practice, it cannot be careless at all, and we still treat everything with a serious attitude as if it were a valuable thing. We hope that in the future, the readers of this column will all try to do the same work, apply the theories they have learned to dissect and criticize a specific political, economic, or social problem, or apply them to a famous work, a famous novel, a play, a film, a suicide, "love," "plagiarism," "kidnapping," and so on, to verify what you have learned and strengthen your power of understanding.

Having explained the above, we believe that readers will feel more cordial when reading the following text.

Now let's return to the case study of the Northeast problem.

There are naturally many methods to study the Northeast problem. But they can be roughly summarized into two types: one method is to observe from a static, isolated, and subjective perspective; the other is to observe from a dynamic, process-oriented, connected, and objective perspective. In each of these two methods, because some people focus on a certain aspect, or mechanically apply the rules, different conclusions can also be drawn, resulting in very chaotic phenomena. However, those who truly grasp the essence of science will not be confused by this chaotic phenomenon.

Let's briefly talk about the first method of observation.

Many advanced Chinese scholars believe that the occurrence of the Northeast problem is due to the ambition of the Japanese militarists; and it is only a local problem in China. Therefore, they hope that the Japanese military will realize their mistakes, hope that the Japanese proletariat will rise up in revolution, hope that the League of Nations will uphold justice, and hope that the people will remain calm, slowly making the Japanese realize their mistakes, and hope to seek a solution through diplomatic channels. Another group of smarter scholars even want to lure Japan to attack the Soviet Union, in order to reduce Japanese oppression. They believe that the Japanese are encroaching step by step because the "bandits" have betrayed the nation and dispersed the anti-Japanese forces. They believe that there is no possibility of resisting Japan at present, and at least ten years must be waited (as Dr. Hu Shi said). Therefore, now we can only talk about construction and cultivating national strength.

For these gentlemen's high opinions, naturally, there is no need to spend any more effort to explain them here. Iron facts have already exposed their hypocrisy. However, these "high opinions," no matter how naive and absurd, are not without reason. It is still a conclusion under a certain method of observation. Although it is the interests of their group that determine them to adopt this view, this view can paralyze many young people who are pursuing the truth. For example, Mr. Fang is undoubtedly one of them.

The second method of observation is to observe the occurrence, development, and solution of the problem in the following relationships:

(1) In the mutual relationship of the international (referring to the capitalist system), that is, in the opposition between imperialism and imperialist countries, more specifically, in the deepening of the world economic panic and the struggle for power among the imperialists in the Pacific, to understand the basis for the occurrence of this problem.

(2) Understand the crisis of the Chinese nation in the relationship of opposition between imperialism and colonies.

(3) Understand the anti-Soviet war and the suppression of the Chinese national revolutionary movement in the relationship of opposition between the two major systems of capitalism and socialism.

The Northeast problem is a product of the synthesis of the above three groups of oppositions. To study the Northeast problem, not only can we not take the first subjective form of research method, but also we cannot only take any part of the second research method and mechanically apply it. Because the complexity of the Northeast problem is precisely caused by the intersection of these three groups of oppositions. Only by understanding this complexity, understanding the basis for creating this complexity, can we talk about correctly studying the Northeast and recognizing the seriousness of this problem. Only then can we talk about how to correctly lead the Chinese people to resist Japan and save the country.

However, it is not enough to simply grasp the root cause of the problem, because recent international events are constantly changing. Although the opposition of these three groups is still sharply reflected in the Northeast and the whole of China, it is also very sensitive to reflect on this problem due to changes in the balance of world economic, political, and social forces. This makes the problem even more complicated. This is very easy to understand. Compared with the day of "September 18th" and now, the relationship at that time was naturally simpler than now, and its seriousness is not as frightening as it is now. When we study the Northeast problem today, we must also judge the relationship of the past few years on top of it, so that the problem can be understood in the most realistic way.

The above is just a brief indication of some principles. Below, we will apply the above principles to the problem itself and implement the dissection of the problem itself. At the same time, in order to make it easier for readers to understand, in the writing of the dissection, we will specifically put forward the wonderful arguments of formal observers as a comparison and send them to the yesterday of the times. (To be continued)

Letter 170

To the Editor, Yesterday I read a news item in your newspaper's local news column about a dispute over the use of private houses to run a nursery. It said, "The day before yesterday, Yang Maorong even accompanied the patrol officer of the Second District, Second Precinct to force the tenants to move out, causing dissatisfaction among the tenants and arousing public anger. It is now learned that the tenants have united to deal with the situation, etc." I am very surprised. The houses at Nos. 1 to 7 Pinfang Lane were originally municipal property, not private houses. The Children's Welfare Committee had already submitted a request to the municipal government to allocate them for the establishment of a nursery. The Second District, Second Precinct had notified the tenants of these houses twice on the 3rd and 21st of last month to move out within a month. On the 10th of this month, the Finance Bureau also sent staff members Cheng Fengyun and Hu Jixing, accompanied by Patrol Officer Tu of the Second District, Second Precinct, and Maorong, to hand over and take over the houses and verbally informed the tenants to move out as scheduled so that the nursery could be opened as soon as possible. This is a matter of handling affairs according to regulations and is imperative. There was no coercion at the time, and there was no arousal of public anger. However, your newspaper reported that the use of private houses aroused public anger. It is regrettable that it hinders personal reputation is a small matter, but the impact on the opening of the nursery and the obstruction of the development of public welfare is great. I am writing to request a correction. Yours sincerely, Yang Maorong, March 22nd.

To the Esteemed Editor, I read in your newspaper on the 21st of this month the conversation of Mr. Lang Guanpu, saying, "The old troops of Ma Zhanshan have gradually been reorganized by others, and only Tan Zixin's 2,000 or so men remain, now stationed in Henan and under the command of Liu Zhi, etc." Jianhua came to Shanghai from Henan Province not long ago. General Tan's troops fought bloody battles in the Northeast for many years. Last winter, they were reorganized by the Central Government into a division. Recently, due to financial difficulties, more than 2,000 men were cut off. The name is the 10th Cavalry Division, which is currently suppressing bandits on the front line. The relationship with the officials and people of Henan Province is very good. Jianhua was stationed in the headquarters of the division when he was in Henan and knows a lot about it. What Mr. Lang said is too far from the truth, and I am afraid it will lead to misunderstandings from the outside world. I have to trouble the esteemed editor to grant a correction. Thank you, thank you. Yours respectfully, Tao Jianhua.

Spring and Autumn

Rising at Dawn 171

— Xianxian

In this era when the long night is still long and dawn is yet to come, someone has actually initiated a dawn movement. The reason is that rising at dawn allows one to absorb a few breaths of fresh air, storing them in the belly, so as not to be timid and sluggish when doing things.

Indeed, after China has rejuvenated from an old empire to become a youthful China, naturally, everything should be vigorous and energetic, so as not to fall behind and be swallowed by the times.

The so-called vigor naturally means that when doing things, one should avoid being fussy and should not groan without illness.

The plan for the year lies in spring, and the plan for the day lies in the morning. Rising at dawn is naturally a great principle. However, since rising at dawn has become a movement, then I think it should also set some work after rising at dawn, and it does not seem to be limited to sweeping the courtyard, practicing a few sets of Taijiquan, or proclaiming a burst of Amitabha Buddha's name, or, like people of leisure, taking a lark or hibiscus to the City God Temple for tea. In my humble opinion, it is better not to initiate a dawn movement. If you want to initiate a dawn movement, you should move the office hours to sunrise. Because at that time, the earth is full of vigor, and everyone works in the strong vigor, and the service spirit will naturally be nurtured in the vigor, and everything will be seen as having a vigorous spirit. - This is always much better than rising at dawn, enjoying the vigor, storing the vigor in the belly and slowly exhaling it again, and dissolving it into the work. This is stronger than the rule of holding morning meetings on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays, and being punished if you are absent three times, because although morning meetings are held on Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays, on Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Saturdays, it is inevitable to stay in bed grandiosely. What is this all about?

In the old monarchical era, good emperors were the ones who went to court at 3 a.m. with palace maids holding red gauze lanterns. From then on, the emperor did not go to court early, and from then on, there were many troubles in the world. It can be seen that rising at dawn is indeed very reasonable.

The long night is still long, and dawn is yet to come. When dawn arrives, let us all rise up and strive forward in the vigor.

Feces! 172

— Old Farmer

This may surprise everyone, we eat feces every day, but I want to ask; can we go without rice for a day, or without vegetables for a day? If your answer is "no," then I conclude that you must be eating feces, because most of the things we eat every day are grown with feces and urine.

Our country has been using feces and urine as fertilizer for thousands of years. Except for the young masters and ladies who live in the city and do not know the five grains, probably everyone knows this.

The economic value of feces and urine is staggering. According to the statistics of Professor J.H. Reisner of Jinling University, our country can produce 428.12 million pounds of human feces every year. If two-thirds of it is used as fertilizer, it will be 285.42 million pounds, which is about 214 million dan. If each dan is calculated at an average of one jiao, it is already worth 21.4 million yuan.

Of course, farmers are the ones who live directly on feces, but there are also many merchants who make a fortune from feces. It is said that Wuxi has a particularly large number of outhouses, which is how they make a living. It is said that a family with three outhouses can be free from hunger and cold.

Recently, science has become increasingly prosperous, and the effectiveness of feces has also gradually increased. A famous German scientist named Sindermann has made useful and edible things such as ammonium sulfate, gas, carbon dioxide, pine oil, and fat from feces.

Everyone should no longer look down on human feces. The effectiveness of feces is really great. People generally call feces "golden juice," which is not too much of an exaggeration.

Hence, it is known that separate distances are apart from heavy springs. Because of his critical illness, my admiration increased. Such rivers and mountains flow away in the blink of an eye. When his merits were completed and his body was exhausted, it was most difficult to see him taking the lead in righteousness.

Research on Inkstones (7) 175

— Wuliaoke

Overview of Duan Inkstones

The essence of inkstones, as mentioned earlier, is that among the inkstones in various places, the three types of Duan, She, and Cheng are the most important. Now, let's first discuss these three types, and of course, we must first talk about Duan.

(1) The Difference between Water Rock and Mountain Pit. From the beginning of mining in the early Tang Dynasty to the last excavation by Zhang Zhidong in the Qing Dynasty, there are many records of the years and times of mining and the names of each pit. Those who have studied inkstones a little all know this, so there is no need to repeat them. Generally, the ones opened in the Tang and Song dynasties were: Xia Yan, Zhong Yan, Shang Yan, Long Yan, Half-Mountain Rocks, Bang Pit, Later Licha Garden, General Pit, and Small Xiangxia.

The ones opened in the Ming and Qing dynasties were: Da Xi Dong, Zheng Dong, Xiao Xi Dong, Dong Dong (with Gong Peng, Dong Zi, Miao Wei), all called Shui Yan, which is the Xia Yan called in the Tang and Song dynasties. In addition, those in Xiana, such as Kengzi Yan, Lao Yan, Xuande Yan, Chaotian Yan, Feishu Yan, Wenshu Pit, and Gutayan Pingfengbei, etc., and those in Xianbei, such as Longzhao Yan, Chaojing Yan, and Apokeng, etc., and those in Beiling, such as Baixian Yan, Chanchu Pit, Song Pit, Meihua Pit, and Jinyun Pit, etc., and those on the west bank, such as Su Pit, Dakengtou, and Huwei Pit, etc., are all called Shan Keng. (Only the more famous ones are recorded for Shan Keng)

What I want to talk about now is the first question, which is the difference between Shui Yan and Shan Keng. The Japanese scholar Kogawa Masazakura said in his Inkstone Tan: "Japanese connoisseurs can all recognize the difference between Shui Yan and Shan Keng, but few can further distinguish the advantages and disadvantages of each stone in Shan Keng. If you want to go further and be able to distinguish which is Zheng Dong, which is Dong Dong, and which is Da Xi Xiao Xi in Shui Yan, there are even fewer. As for pointing out which layer of stone each stone in Shui Yan is, it is even more impossible." This is indeed not an easy task. Not to mention Japan, even in our country, only a few elegant officials and literati who personally went to the mountains to purchase and the workers in Huanggang who made a living by opening pits and making inkstones can distinguish them. Since ancient times, there have been many writings discussing the quality and stone properties of inkstones, but there are indeed not many insightful and experienced talks. Only the Duanxi Inkstone History written by Wu Shihua of Jiaying in the Daoguang years is the most accurate and can distinguish the advantages and disadvantages of the four caves of Shui Yan and the five layers of stone in each cave one by one. In the past, there were endless disputes about the advantages and disadvantages of the East and West caves, but later, Da Xi was highly praised. Wu Shihua's discussion is very correct. We believe that the necessary conditions for recognizing the stone of Da Xi Dong or Shui Gui Dong (the deepest part of Da Xi Dong) of Shui Yan are: (1) "Quality": dense texture, fine and smooth, warm and moist as jade, although extremely smooth, it can produce ink, release ink, and remove ink (washing it away without a trace is called removing ink).

(2) "Color": The stone on the north wall of Xia Yan before the Song Dynasty is deep purple like pig liver, moist like purple Lin Yu, and makes no sound when ground (this product is rare). The Shui Yan after the Ming Dynasty is mostly cyan-white and light purple like lamb liver, gentle and soft, like a new spring flowing.

(3) "Sound": When knocked, it sounds like wood. The ancients called it silent, but it is not really silent.

(4) "Beautiful patterns" such as cyan flowers, fish brain, sky blue, fire imprint, banana white, and oriole eyes, etc., must be bright and lively, and the red, white, and green colors must be particularly clear and vivid, like clouds and rosy clouds, with a pure, deep, delicate air. If these conditions are met, it must be a famous stone of Da Xi Dong. Shui Yan is in the water, so it is more moist and waxy. The ancients mystified it and called it "spring-born in stone, not stone-born in spring." Inkstone lovers regard it as a famous saying and supreme theory, but in fact, it is not reasonable.

The Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 176

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Six: Speaking Generously, Forgetting Home and Serving the Country; Sadly Facing the Jade Mirror, Lamenting My Beloved

When Ziqiang thought of this, he scratched his hair with one hand and beat the kang mat with the other, muttering to himself: Forget it, forget it, alas! Wang Shili was lying on the windowsill, filling out a form. Thinking that he had written it wrong, and that he was losing his temper there, he immediately stood up straight and asked: Isn't it written this way? Zhao Ziqiang suddenly heard him shout and realized what was happening. He stood up and asked: What are you talking about? I didn't realize you were in the room. Wang Shili said: Didn't the company commander just say forget it, forget it, was he greeting me? Zhao Ziqiang thought for a moment, shook his head and smiled: I didn't say you at all. I was thinking in my heart that these enemies are really hateful, flying their planes into our airspace as if it were no man's land. We don't have... Suddenly he laughed again and said: This time, we will definitely have planes coming, according to what I know, the number is still quite a lot. Wang Shili said: Since we have planes, why doesn't our air force launch? Zhao Ziqiang laughed and said: I'm just a small company commander, how can I answer you this question? If I were a commander-in-chief, I could answer you this question. Wang Shili said: I think maybe we don't launch the air force first in order to prevent the enemy from preparing, and when it is necessary to launch, we suddenly fly out all of them, two or three hundred planes, lining up in the sky and heading straight to the Northeast, bombing them unexpectedly. At that time, our army will also be more active. Company commander, do you think I guessed right or wrong? Ziqiang rubbed his chin with his hand and smiled slightly: Probably close enough, right? Wang Shili rubbed his hands together, shrugged his shoulders and smiled: If there is such a day, that would be fun. Ziqiang smiled: You do have a patriotic heart. Wang Shili stomped his foot and said: Company commander, don't mention it, I almost caused trouble because of patriotism. Once I went to the Dong'an Market, damn it, I met a large group of dwarfs. World Oddities

— Shuiyu

The World's Largest Book 177

Americans, in order to oppose war, have published a very large book, which has been signed by millions of people. It is seven feet five inches long and three feet five inches wide, with two thousand three hundred and thirty pages. Its content is a description of the "opposition to war" and "peace to save the fundamental of the world economic panic" for the International Disarmament Conference. On the cover, there are large characters engraved, "ＷartheSuperRacktWorldRecoveryDependsonPeace"

The World's Largest Newspaper 178

In the east of Germany, bordering Belgium, there is a town called Aachen. The museum of this town collects all the newspapers in the world. Among them, there is the "Four Major Constellations" newspaper issued in New York in 1859, which is two point two eight six meters long and one point six two eight eight meters wide. The whole newspaper has eight pages. The amount of articles is equal to 400 pages of 46-size version, just like 200 pages of Shen Bao. The entire newspaper is carved with woodblocks and printed by hand. The pre-printed edition is 28,000 copies, and each copy is sold for 50 cents, which is equal to 3 jiao in our country. However, this newspaper is neither a daily nor a weekly. It is issued once every hundred years, so it will be issued for the second time in 1995.

Plane War Against Locusts 179

The government of Argentina in South America invested 300,000 yuan last year to use planes to conquer locusts, because the country suffered a great locust plague last year. The national agricultural production was almost without harvest, and the loss in one year reached 20 million yuan. Therefore, the government decided to use planes to exterminate them, that is, to sprinkle medicine on the grasslands where locusts breed and chase the swarms of locusts in the sky, making the locusts have no place to stay.

The World's Oldest Musical Instrument 180

In the Bolaushan Mountains of Czechoslovakia, a flute made of lion teeth was recently discovered. The discoverer was Professor Claire Yabaishulong of Bruno University. Mr. Ke judged that this flute was a relic of the Water River era 30,000 years ago. However, it can only produce the sounds of D and G, and it is indeed the oldest musical instrument in the world.

The New Great Wall 181

At the Communist Party Congress on the 26th of last month, Chairman Molotov of the Russian People's Committee declared that the military preparations on Russia's eastern border had been completed. However, the security of the western border was very worrying. Recently, a 20th-century Great Wall has been built on the Estonian border. Every considerable distance on the wall has a 30-foot-high watchtower, with complete telegraph and telephone equipment, and is in contact with the headquarters of the border guard. The purpose of this Great Wall is ostensibly to monitor contraband smuggled into Russia from abroad, but in reality, it is to prevent the Russian people from fleeing abroad. Therefore, if people are seen escaping outside the wall from the watchtowers, they can be shot from the towers.

Seventy-Year-Old Elementary School Student 182

In Yamabuki Elementary School in Ushigomi Ward, Tokyo, there is an elementary school first-grader who is already 69 years old. She is a housewife who runs a shoe store in Ichigaya Daimachi. Every day, she walks three miles from home to school. Although her hair has turned white, she is energetic and runs around in the campus with her seven or eight-year-old classmates, forgetting her original appearance.

Exchange of International Goods 183

The original method of exchanging goods is now popular again internationally. For example, South American Brazil exchanges merchant ships with Japan for coffee, exchanges commodities and machinery with England and Poland, and recently ordered warships from British shipyards, also using Brazilian coffee as the price. Similarly, Greece hired technicians from Italy to build warehouses, and their salaries were compensated by exporting cigarettes to Italy.

Educational News from Other Places

Promulgation of Measures by the Ministry of Education for Subsidizing Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast 184

Northeast Youth Education Relief Office Sends Letters to All Schools Nationwide Requesting Applications for Subsidies from Students from the Northeast

(Nanjing Special Dispatch) The Northeast Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry of Education has formulated the "Provisional Measures for Subsidizing Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast." After submitting them to the Ministry of Education for approval, yesterday, it sent separate letters to all provinces, cities, bureaus, and colleges above the vocational level nationwide, requesting them to identify diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast as stipulated in the measures, fill out application forms, and apply to the office for subsidy fees. The original letter stated, "In order to expand educational opportunities and cultivate national salvation forces, the Ministry of Education has formulated twelve Provisional Measures for the Relief of Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast (referring to students from Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and Harbin provinces and cities) who were forced or voluntarily entered the pass to seek education with diligence and ambition. These measures were submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation. In accordance with the provisions of Article 2 of these measures, the Northeast Youth Education Relief Office was established to handle various relief affairs. It was established in Shangjing on January 30 of this year and a resident office was established in Beiping on February 12 to be responsible for investigating diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast in the provinces and cities of North China. In accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the Provisional Measures for the Relief of Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast, relief matters are temporarily divided into four categories: '(A) The Ministry of Education continues to issue notices to all public and private schools at all levels nationwide, stipulating that diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast, who have been verified by the school, shall be exempt from tuition fees; (B) Subsidies shall be granted to those who are truly unable to afford meals, accommodation, books, etc., but have excellent academic performance; (C) Schools shall be established specifically for training students from the Northeast; (D) A quota shall be set for students from the Northeast studying abroad.' Except for A, C, and D, which have been handled separately, the granting of subsidies under category B has also been drafted by this office as Provisional Measures for Subsidizing Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast and submitted to the Ministry of Education, which approved it under Order No. 1911. In addition to sending separate letters, we enclose a copy of the Provisional Measures for Subsidizing Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast, as well as an application form, a guarantee letter, and a certificate, and send them to your 'Department,' 'Bureau,' 'School' for reference and distribution to your affiliated colleges and attached schools. Please thoroughly investigate the diligent and hardworking students from the Northeast who are currently studying. Those who meet the provisions of Article 1 of the Provisional Measures for Subsidizing Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast should be instructed to fill out the application form, sign and seal it, attach a recent two-and-a-half-inch headshot, and obtain a guarantee letter from two individuals with considerable occupations or reliable credit. After verification by the college, fill out the official certificate and send it directly to this office (those closer to Nanjing, please send it to this office in Nanjing; those closer to Beiping, please send it to the resident office of this office on Dangbu Street, Beiping City) for verification and handling. This is for official communication."

Subsidies from the Northeast Youth Education Relief Office

Provisional Measures for Subsidizing Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast

(1) Students from Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and Harbin provinces and cities who have entered the pass to seek education with diligence and ambition, who meet the qualifications stipulated in Category B of Article 3 of the Provisional Measures for the Relief of Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast, and who have been verified by the school they are attending and granted tuition exemption, may apply to this office for subsidy fees.

(2) Students applying for subsidies under the preceding paragraph shall fill out an application form, sign and seal it, attach a recent two-and-a-half-inch headshot, and obtain a guarantee letter from two individuals with considerable occupations or reliable credit and an official certificate from the school they are currently attending. (This application form, guarantee letter, and certificate shall be printed by this office, distributed to various schools, and forwarded for use.) They shall be submitted by the school they are attending to this office for verification and handling.

(3) This office shall thoroughly investigate the facts listed in the application form, guarantee letter, and certificate in the preceding paragraph and submit them, together with the results of the investigation, to the review committee for thorough review in accordance with the prescribed standards and procedures.

(4) For students who have been reviewed by the review committee, this office may, if it deems necessary, conduct an examination in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 of the Provisional Measures for the Relief of Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast to determine the granting of subsidy fees. The examination affairs shall be handled by a committee organized by this office in accordance with Article 7 of the organizational regulations.

(5) Students who have passed the review or examination must be submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval before they can be formally recognized as students subsidized by this office.

(6) The quota of subsidized students and the amount of subsidy fees for each level of school shall be temporarily handled in accordance with the following regulations. However, if it is necessary to increase or decrease the quota during implementation, this office may submit a request to the Ministry of Education for appropriate changes.

Students above the junior high school level who have already received meals or meal subsidies from the school or organization shall not be eligible for ordinary subsidy fees. Those who receive other types of subsidies or relief in addition to meals shall not be eligible for special subsidy fees. In addition, those who have not received any other subsidies or relief and are truly unable to afford meals, accommodation, books, etc., but have excellent academic performance, may apply for ordinary subsidy fees and also apply for special subsidy fees if they meet the provisions of Article 1 of these measures.

School Type　Ordinary Subsidy Quota　(Meal Subsidy) Amount　Special Subsidy Quota　(Book and Daily Use Subsidy) Amount　Monthly Expenditure Amount

Elementary School　1,000 students　3 yuan per semester　　500 yuan

Junior High School and Equivalent Schools　800 students　3.5 yuan per month　250 students　2 yuan per month　3,300 yuan

Senior High School and Equivalent Schools　900 students　3.5 yuan per month　350 students　3 yuan per month　4,200 yuan

Colleges and Above　900 students　4 yuan per month　480 students　5 yuan per month　6,000 yuan

Total　2,600 students　2,080 students　14,000 yuan

(7) The monthly subsidy fees to be received by each subsidized student shall be sent by this office to the school they are currently attending for forwarding to the student for verification and receipt. A receipt signed and sealed by the student in person shall be sent to this office for reporting to the Ministry of Education. However, this office may send personnel to assist in the disbursement of funds by the schools to ensure prudence.

(8) Subsidized students who return home during the holidays shall have their subsidy fees for the holidays deducted.

(9) Subsidized students shall abide by the management regulations of this office and other regulations and orders. If any of the circumstances listed in Article 9 of the Provisional Measures for the Relief of Diligent and Hardworking Students from the Northeast occur, their eligibility to receive subsidy fees shall be immediately revoked. Those with more serious circumstances shall also have their already received subsidy fees recovered.

(10) These measures shall be implemented from the date they are approved by the Ministry of Education and shall be abolished on July 31, 1934.

Category B of Article 3: Subsidies shall be granted to those who are truly unable to afford meals, accommodation, books, etc., but have excellent academic performance.

Article 9: Any student from the Northeast who receives relief under the above articles shall have their eligibility for relief revoked if any of the following circumstances occur. Those with more serious circumstances shall also have the benefits they have already received recovered. Separate management regulations shall be formulated.

(A) Those who violate school rules and are expelled from school or have received two major demerits;

(B) Those who repeat a grade twice during their studies;

(C) Those who do not comply with the rules and orders of the relief office;

(D) Those who have acted in a manner that disrespects national honor and interests;

Discussions on Education Issues Between Ministry of Education Officials and Mr. Mowrer 185

China Must Establish Vocational Schools That Meet Needs

Efforts Should Be Made to Promote Elementary Education

Mr. Mowrer, Deputy Director of the International Labor Office, accompanied by Mr. Li Ximou, Commissioner of the Ministry of Education, and others, arrived at the Ministry of Education at around 4:00 p.m. on the 20th to discuss education issues. Minister of Education Wang Shijie invited Vice Ministers, Directors of various departments, Secretaries, Counselors, Section Chiefs, etc., to gather in one room. He first expressed his welcome and then exchanged views and reports on education issues. Mr. Mowrer said that although his stay in China has not been long, based on his observations, the most urgent need for education in China at present is to vigorously develop vocational education and to establish practical vocational schools that are not merely for show and that meet the needs. In order to promote the popularization of education, efforts should be made to promote elementary education. These were Mr. Mowrer's suggestions for China to pay attention to promoting vocational education and elementary education. He then asked about the Chinese education community's feelings regarding the recommendations on education in the report of the previous League of Nations inspection team. In addition to Vice Minister of Education Duan Xipeng reporting on the implementation of higher, secondary, and elementary education in the Ministry of Education in the past two years and the direction taken by Chinese education, he responded to Mr. Mowrer's inquiry about the recommendations in the report, saying that China has many similar plans to the League of Nations report and is currently carrying out these plans. Except for a small part that is difficult due to factual difficulties and national conditions in China and cannot be proportional, most of them are agreed with and accepted. As for the teaching of China to promote vocational education and elementary education, the Ministry of Education has plans and methods to promote them nationwide so as to gradually achieve expectations. It is also heard that Mr. Mowrer will still go to the Ministry of Education on the 22nd to discuss more specific education issues.

Explanation by the Ministry of Education on the Measures for Examining and Grading Student Performance in Primary and Secondary Schools 188

The Ministry of Education, based on the inquiry from the Hebei Provincial Department of Education, asked whether the measures for examining and grading student academic performance in secondary schools and elementary schools during peacetime by educational administrative organs at all levels also included normal vocational schools. (The draft measures issued by the Ministry for secondary schools include middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. However, according to the provisions of Article 5 of the original measures, it seems to only refer to middle schools. Does this measure also apply to normal vocational schools?) It was instructed to explain, "The measures for examining and grading student academic performance in secondary schools and elementary schools during peacetime by educational administrative organs at all levels issued by this Ministry naturally include middle schools, elementary schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. Article 5 of the original measures is specifically intended to supplement the measures for graduation examinations in middle schools, with special emphasis on middle schools and subjects that have not been examined and subjects with poor examination results. This provision does not exclude the peacetime examination of student academic performance in normal and vocational schools. Please be informed."

Celebration Ceremony for This Year's Children's Day Held at the Municipal Government 190

Mayor Wu Receives Children and Distributes Souvenirs

The Shanghai Children's Airplane Will Perform at the Venue

Government Agencies, Movie Theaters, and Public and Private Parks Open to Treat Children

Representatives from Schools and Factories Participate

April 4th is China's National Children's Day. The city's party and government agencies have organized a Children's Day Preparatory Committee to prepare for the celebration of Children's Day. The committee held its second preparatory committee meeting at 10:00 a.m. yesterday in the second conference room of the Education Bureau in the city center. The committee members present included Hu Shuyi from the Children's Welfare Association, Lu Hailan and Zhang Zhu from the Education Bureau, Yang Zhi, Yin Guanzhi from the Public Security Bureau, Qiu Xisheng from the Social Affairs Bureau, Cai Hongtian from the Municipal Party Headquarters (on behalf of Hu), Sun Jiaqi from the Health Bureau (on behalf of Hu), and Chairman Hu Shuyi.

Reporting Matters: Chairman Hu Shuyi first read the resolutions of the previous meeting and asked the committee members to report on the matters they had taken over. Cai Hongtian then reported on the progress of contacting various agencies to open to the public for children to visit within a week after Children's Day. Committee member Qiu Xisheng reported on the plan to invite children in the city to visit the city center area and the progress of contacting parks and private gardens to open to the public. Committee members Lu Hailan and Yin Guanzhi reported on the progress of contacting various cinemas to screen children's educational films. Committee member Hu Shuyi reported on the progress of contacting the Newspaper Association to have major newspapers publish special issues for Children's Day and contacting the Book Industry Association to sell books to children at low prices within a week starting from Children's Day.

Job Assignments: Then, matters for discussion: (1) A proposal to assign positions to the committee members. The resolution was: (A) To invite Director Pan of the Education Bureau to serve as the chairman of the committee; (B) To invite committee members Hu Shuyi, Sun Jiaqi, and Yang Zhi to handle the general affairs of the committee; (C) To invite committee member Zhang Zhu to handle the document affairs of the committee; (D) To invite committee members Cai Hongtian, Hu Shuyi, Zhang Zhu, and Zhou Wei to handle the publicity affairs of the committee; (E) To invite committee members Yin Guanzhi, Qiu Xisheng, and representatives from the China Children's Welfare Association to handle the communication affairs of the committee; (F) To invite committee members Lu Hailan and Zhang Zhu to contact the Municipal People's Education Hall to prepare for the committee's exhibition and entertainment performances.

Celebration Procedures: (2) The decision on the Children's Day celebration procedures and the contact with administrative personnel. The resolution was: (A) The celebration ceremony will be held at 10:00 a.m. in the auditorium of the Municipal Government. The procedures are as follows: (1) Music playing (2) Singing the party song (3) Bowing in the highest respect to the party's national flag and the portrait of the Premier (4) Silent tribute (5) Chairman's report (Chairman Zhou, Mayor, the four Bureau Directors of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Education, Public Security, Social Affairs, and Health, and the Children's Welfare Committee) (6) Speech by a celebrity (7) Speech by a child representative (8) Distribution of Children's Day gifts (9) Completion of the ceremony, music playing (10) Mayor's reception of children and distribution of Children's Day souvenirs (11) Performance by the Shanghai Children's Airplane (12) Invitation for children to visit the Municipal Government and various bureaus (13) Invitation for children to visit parks (Municipal First Park, Confucius Temple Park, Zoo, Bansongyuan, Jiangwan Ye Garden, Zhaofeng Park, Hongkou Park, Bund Park, Gujiazhai Park). The Children's Welfare Association will print free park visit coupons and distribute them to the children. (14) Radio broadcast (at 5:00 p.m., please have committee member Hu Shuyi report) (15) People's Education Hall exhibition and entertainment show (16) Adjournment. (B) The committee will prepare a letter to be delivered by committee member Yin Guanzhi to the Public Security Bureau to contact the band. (C) The committee will prepare letters to be delivered by the China Children's Welfare Association and committee member Qiu Xisheng to contact Ma Xiangbo, Wu Zhihui, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Shizeng, and Kong Xiangxi for speeches by celebrities. (D) Please have committee member Yang Zhi contact the child representative for the speech.

Number of Representatives: (3) A decision on the number of representatives from each school to participate in the Children's Day celebration ceremony. The resolution was to instruct the municipal and private registered elementary schools to nominate two representatives from each grade, and to notify other unregistered elementary schools to nominate representatives in the same way, led by teachers from each school to participate in the Municipal Government. (4) A decision to invite children under the age of 15 from various factories and workers to participate in the Children's Day celebration ceremony. The resolution was to instruct the Social Affairs Bureau to have each labor union send five to thirty children under the age of 15 of workers to participate and to have the labor union send people to take care of them at the Municipal Government. (5) A decision to notify charitable organizations in the city that accommodate children to participate in the celebration ceremony held at the Municipal Government on Children's Day. The resolution was to be handled by the Social Affairs Bureau.

Other Matters: (6) To have the committee notify the Public Utilities Bureau to instruct the public bus company to transport children to and from the Municipal Government for the Children's Day celebration ceremony at half the usual price. The resolution was passed and the committee will prepare a letter to be delivered by committee member Yin Guanzhi to contact. (7) Several nurses should be invited to the Municipal Government to take care of the children on Children's Day. The resolution was to be handled by the Health Bureau. (8) Police should be sent to the venue on Children's Day to take care of the children. The resolution was to be handled by the Public Security Bureau. (9) Tea and snacks should be prepared at the Municipal Government for the children on Children's Day. The resolution was to be handled by the Children's Welfare Committee. (10) Because this year's Children's Day celebration ceremony is held at the Municipal Government, for the convenience of handling affairs, it is proposed to invite personnel from the First and Third Sections of the Municipal Government to attend and join the preparatory committee. The resolution was passed and the committee will send a letter inviting the Municipal Government to send personnel to participate. (11) Because of the urgent time for the preparations for this year's Children's Day celebration, the funds cannot be submitted jointly by the four bureaus to the Municipal Government for allocation. Pang Jingzhou Returns to Shanghai After Inspecting North China Medical College 192

Dr. Pang Jingzhou, who was hired by the Ministry of Education, left Shanghai on the 5th of this month to inspect the state of medical education in North China in Jinan, Beiping, Baoding, Kaifeng, and other places. He has now returned to Shanghai after completing his public duties and is resuming his regular medical practice. According to Mr. Pang, students in various places in North China are able to endure hardship, and the lives of teachers are also relatively stable, so the spirit of each school has special merits. However, the customs of the people are relatively closed, and patients who are hospitalized are generally perceived to be lacking, which poses a major difficulty for the clinical work of the medical school. As for his detailed report, it is currently being organized and will soon be submitted to the Ministry of Education.

Superb Skill　The situation in yesterday's battle was tense, the movements were swift, and the interest was very strong. The Chinese women were lively and exquisite, and their performance was superb. The forwards were sharp and extraordinary, seizing every opportunity. Chen Rongming's technique was skillful, and her eyes were focused. Several long shots were incredibly skillful, leaving the audience in awe. The guards suffered due to their short stature, and there were occasional risks. Fortunately, their ball skills were pure, and they took the initiative, preventing the opponent from shooting. In terms of passing and shooting, the Chinese team was above Great Britain. Moreover, their liveliness and fighting spirit, their elusive movements, were unmatched by their opponents. Great Britain relied solely on their tall physique, but their technique was slow and rigid, and not worth learning from. Only two or three hundred people watched, and the appeal did not seem to be great.

Key to Victory　The overall momentum was tense and extremely fierce. The Chinese team was well-balanced, but Chen Juming stood out from the crowd and was the hero of the victory. Great Britain's Parker Hill and Hugh Leighton were also very skilled. At the beginning, Great Britain showed its edge, but the Chinese team advanced step by step, slowly expanding their lead. They took the lead 8-7 in the first quarter. From the second quarter, the Chinese team's score increased significantly, but Great Britain eventually caught up, making it 18-16. The Chinese team only led by two points in the first half. The key to victory was entirely in the third quarter, where China scored a total of eleven points, while the opponent only scored three points. Even if Great Britain counterattacked in the end, they were still out of reach.

One Point Ahead　The United States took the lead with a surprise attack. The center jumped for the ball, and the guard received it, sending it to the basket. V. Poring and Parker Hill each scored a goal, surprising China. The defense was then strengthened. Yang Sen made one free throw, also scoring three points. V. Poring scored again, making the score 7-3. The British women were overjoyed. The Chinese team quickly caught up, and the forwards gradually coordinated. Chen Rongming refused to be outdone, making close and long-range shots, showing off her skills. In an instant, she scored five points in a row, exciting the audience and cheering them on. British player Parker injured her foot and left the field, replaced by Haymont. The first quarter ended with China winning by one point, 8-7.

Sometimes Strong, Sometimes Weak　Parker continued to play, and the Chinese team's edge was strong and unmatched. The forwards became more active, and the defense became more strict. After Chen Jucai scored first, Yang Sen and Chen Rongming successively made contributions, and the score increased greatly. They ran across the field, like hungry tigers. The British women were greatly threatened and frustrated for a long time. However, their determination to advance did not slacken. At 7-18, after a stalemate, the British team also followed closely, pressing hard. The situation suddenly changed, and B. Poring made a free throw, turning a spark into a prairie fire. Afterwards, Parker Hill and others scored four goals in a row, and the score changed to 18-16, with China only leading by two points.

Golden Age　In the second quarter, the biggest score difference was when China was ahead by eleven points. It was undoubtedly China's golden age. At the beginning of the second half, the United States scored first, making it 18-18. Chen Rongming made three shots in a row, which were wonderful and unmatched. She became more and more courageous in battle, and her arrogance was blazing. Chen and Yang scored successively, and the momentum was magnificent. This was China's golden age, 29-19, a difference of ten points. China's foundation was solid, and victory was already in sight.

Final Victory　In the last quarter, Great Britain counterattacked fiercely, but their shooting was inaccurate. After being monitored and occupied by China, they could not find a way to move, so they had few opportunities to shoot. The great opportunity was missed again and again. The Chinese line was quite chaotic, and the situation was not as good as before. Both sides scored alternately, but the performance was dull and tasteless. Great Britain's fierce counterattack made China feel scared. In the last quarter, Great Britain won by three points, 8-5. In the final result, China won 34-27.

Free Talk

Boredom 203

— Moteng

Most modern youths who are excessively refined and bookish are useless because when it comes to doing things, they can only verbally instruct others. For example, if a robber breaks into the house, they cannot "capture the thief themselves," so they must let the robbers loot the house!

To capture the thief yourself requires skill because thieves are not easy to catch. Even Tai Chi requires skill. There is a great difference between foolishness and wisdom, which is not easy to discern.

Moreover, when the Great Way is abandoned, there is benevolence and righteousness; when poetry dies, then the Spring and Autumn Annals are written; when hermits arise, then the Buddhist dharma declines; when humor arises, then right and wrong die. The reason for this is out of necessity. Everyone feels bored, buzzing and grumbling, and there is no way out. So, what to do? Change the broth.

George Bernard Shaw seems to have described a layer of hell—very different from what Yan Liben painted—where there are no evil ghosts or yakshas, and the ghosts are like floating smoke. There is an age problem there. Pretending to be a seventeen or eighteen-year-old girl is no longer fashionable. It is better to change into a fashionable outfit. Then, the age is over thirty! It is considered more modern. In short, you have to change the look, break the mediocrity and monotony of the atmosphere. It is like a goldfish in a glass tank, unable to swim out of the surrounding transparent substance, so let's swing the tail a few times in there, so be it!

The "romanticism" and "elegance" of some officials are mostly cultivated and forced out in this way. They won't eat vegetables unless they are made by a certain chef, and they must use certain materials to make clothes. When spring comes, they must visit the plum blossoms, and when autumn is deep, they must appreciate the chrysanthemums. This can relieve boredom and resentment, and the risk is relatively small. In a severe drought, fish moisten each other with saliva, but if there is no saliva left, then they will probably all dry up and become dried fish.

Alas! Things have no permanence. Words are forgotten as soon as they are spoken. After being full, one becomes hungry again. Yesterday you captured the thief yourself, and today you have to capture the thief again. Thieves cannot be caught completely, like morphine needles, which must be injected again and again. This is called having no way out. "Oh, my beloved compatriots"! Listen to the "Hang Oh" and wooden fish sounds from the wall!

Spring and Women 204

— Mengzhen

(1)

Spring has arrived, in the gorgeous new clothes of women, in the touching eyebrows of women. "Spring feelings penetrate the crisp chest, spring colors cross the eyebrows." It is spring that has come to the world.

Only I am still wearing a broken cotton robe, which the spring breeze cannot reach. But seeing the dazzling spring light and the spring colors all over the street, the heart of a withered winter also can't help but throb a little.

I walked to a department store and saw the gorgeously dressed, flowery female clerks standing among the colorful goods. She is a kind of moving advertisement.

I strolled through the streets and saw groups of three or five girls on the road, slender figures, brightly colored cheongsams; a woven waist, a semi-circular arm shadow, swaying and swimming, just like the five-colored fish in Yuquan.

In the past, women were only objects of sexual desire, reproductive machines, but now they are more of a work of art for people to admire. Works of art are precious and easily damaged, so I see on women's bodies, strips of paper written by etiquette and morality, warning people in general:

"Look with your eyes, don't touch with your hands!"

Hands off!

(2)

Speaking of works of art, women are not historical rarities like antiques, but fashionable works of art like the recent expressionist and cubist art. On the bodies of women, there is a full meaning of time.

When spring comes, women are the expression of spring in nature, a symbol of spring.

Because they are so full of temporality, the Twin Sister brand of cosmetics, like the beauty trademarks in cigarettes, used to be popular for a lifetime, and were the so-called standards of beauty, but now they have become antiques, outdated things.

For this reason, Confucius said: "Only women and petty people are difficult to raise." This means that modern men and women are easily outdated. A woman's youth is at most only ten years—from fifteen to twenty-five—after this time, "green leaves become shade and the branches are full of children," it is no longer a sunny spring scene where miscellaneous flowers grow and many orioles fly.

Lu Tong's daughter's song says: "Orioles and flowers are blooming, but you don't come, and when you come, the flowers are old," so the late beauty is the most sad thing in life. For this reason, women in general can indeed seize the spring light and are not willing to let this flowery age pass by. Isn't that right? The spring cold is still harsh, spring is just coming, men still have more cotton clothes, and women are all fluttering in single cheongsams. Women can indeed catch up and get the first of the trend. In this respect; women are thoroughly and thoroughly pioneers, they come to the world with spring. Moreover, just as spring symbolizes the germination of all things, women are the producers of mankind.

My Purpose (Continued) 205

— He Jiahua

(8) Gambling Den—I changed it in Xiaoshan, at that time it was when the Japanese imperialists were ravaging Shanghai. Although this is a prose-style thing, I also added about 3,000 words. This manuscript was sent to Modern, but the editor thought that the material was neither like prose nor like a novel, so it was returned; it was later published in Youth World.

The other three articles were changed relatively little, so I will not list them one by one. Under this kind of fact, Zhuanpeng一口咬定 that I "took" his article without his permission, I really don't know what his intention is. In fact, after he already knew the news of Wen Lie, he even asked me to take an article to Liangyou in the afternoon, saying that he needed money to use right away, and asked me if it was okay to sign my name for convenience. I didn't agree at the time. I now understand what his "knowing and doing it" means.

But no matter what, my past casualness about creation is an unforgivable mistake. Although I spent a lot of effort to revise it, so that Zhuanpeng's article completely changed its old appearance, I don't want to argue strongly and try to cover up the sins of the three of us like last time. In addition to Zhuanpeng's article, I also revised two novels by Mr. Chen Fuxi and took one by Mr. Lou Zhiming, which I also frankly admit. Moreover, just like Zhuanpeng pointed out my mistakes, I also hope that he can sincerely correct his behavior that is similar to mine: (1) The Naked Woman Under the Sun, written by Lawrence, originally translated by Mr. Zhou Guangxi, published in the Nanjing Central Daily News; (2) The University Prince, published in the Hangzhou Republic Daily, was written by Chuan Shangao; (3) He asked Peng Chenghui for two volumes of Wen Zichuan's essays, saying that he would send them to Central Park for publication; (4) He also asked Chen Fuxi and Lou Zhiming for novels, which he would not explain in his confession. I am not holding a grudge to report him, but using this fact to illustrate that this ugliness is not my personal problem, but the traditional vanity—the writer's desire—that forms this fact. This vanity made me try to deny this matter at the beginning, which resulted in that article "About My Creation."

But the facts tell me that this kind of cover-up can only be effective when the interests are the same, otherwise it will explode sooner or later. Therefore, I deeply realize that the exposure of this ugliness, superficially speaking, damages my personality and reputation, but in fact, even if I maintain this false personality and honor, it is only harming myself. I am young, I should have self-confidence, so now I am very frank to admit my mistakes. That is to say, this kind of vanity of a writer is just a poison in my life, and I am willing to give myself an injection to clear the poison. But here, I have to solemnly declare that I do not necessarily give up creation. However, my future creative attitude will be serious and faithful. I will never sing that empty tune of "creating for the sake of creation" again, but I want to seek the way of expression from the social significance. I feel empty and small about my present and past self, but I will never be discouraged because of this. I should be vigilant and obtain the practical meaning of creation from life. I hope that I can be silent for a while, if possible.

As for the threats from Yang Cunren and others, I will absolutely not feel terrified, even though they said in the letter to Mr. Chen Fuxi:

"This matter involves Xu Jun, He Jun, and Mr. three people. To be honest, if it is made public, it will be unfavorable to all three of you, especially He Jun..."

Dai Hengjun openly protected Zhuanpeng, saying that he "has another explanation"; such a clever statement, although very beautiful, still cannot hide from the eyes and ears of discerning readers.

In short, I have recognized the significance of this fact from the root of the social system, so I frankly admit that my article "About My Creation" is not frank, and I am exposing my own mistakes to the readers, hoping to get a fair criticism. As for those threats and malicious attacks, I don't have so much free time to pay attention to them.

This is my statement.

Random Notes from the West (2) 207

— Lu Yan

"Damn it!" He seemed about to reach out his fist. "Are you taking it to beg for food! You even want to steal a bowl..." He walked back and forth, grinding his teeth.

He is really a true northerner.

The car finally moved forward. After passing through a few high arch-like iron frames, it stopped in a ship. Walking down to see it, it was not very big. There were a total of four rows, which could only hold twelve carriages. The locomotive put down the four carriages in front of us, then went back to drag four more, and finally dragged the remaining two. When we arrived on the other side, we did this three times. We arrived in Nanjing at 7:45 and did not leave Pukou until 11:00. I thought it was too slow. According to the previous method, I believe that in this time, we can travel back and forth from Nanjing to Pukou two or three times. This great ferry gave us physical comfort, without having to go up and down, but at the same time it gave us spiritual anxiety, making us wait anxiously. It also reduced the carrying fees of our luggage a little, but at the same time it also reduced the income of those coolies.

Now I have been brought to the north of the Yangtze River. Looking out from the car window, I can only see yellow soil and wheat.

Hunan Mountain Songs 208

— Heartfelt Words

(1)

Early in the morning, the dew is heavy,

Wetting my purse and handkerchief.

Wet handkerchief is no matter;

But wetting the purse, ah,

Wastes my sister's money and worries her heart!

(2)

The sun sets behind the mountain ridge,

The spring water behind the ridge is cold and clear;

I advise you, sister, don't drink the cold spring water,

Cold spring water chills the conscience,

Leading to a marriage without offspring!

Miao. I don't know if it's psychological, or a real fact, but I always feel there are no interesting country views. I remember last summer, sitting in a car to Suzhou, the slightly yellow rice and the bright green bean leaves rolled like wheels under my eyes, how interesting it was!

3. On the Longhai Road

Arriving in Xuzhou, I missed several old friends here. It's been more than a decade since I set foot on this land. How did these ten years pass? Like a dream. Where is the youthful banquet? Some have died, and some have disappeared. At least I wanted to take a look at this long-lost homeland. But the night was dark, there was nothing, just a few dim lights, like ghosts.

The passengers in the car now have completely changed their appearance. Their skin is all rough and old, not one of them looks young. Gray or black clothes, reflecting bronze complexions. Men and women, all tightly wrapped their trouser legs. Occasionally, the pungent smell of garlic wafted through the carriage. Although these many people came from different places, their clothes and luggage were almost all domestic products, with no trace of foreign style or southern elegance. I felt like I was seeing the real Chinese people.

The ticket inspectors came to bother us at every stop, I don't know what it means. I had just fallen asleep, and I was woken up. Just now a five- or six-year-old child didn't buy a ticket, but now a three- or four-year-old must buy a ticket.

"Four and a half years old requires a half-price ticket! That's the regulation!"

So the passenger had nothing to say but to take out the money.

"He has no way of knowing how old you really are!" A soldier who followed the ticket inspector said, after they finished checking the tickets, they came again after a small station. Now it was the turn of a village woman who had just gotten on. She was with a three- or four-year-old child. She refused to pay for the ticket, she said that she had taken this car a month ago, and she brought this child, and she didn't buy a half-price ticket either. But she said the child was four years old.

"If you're four years old, you have to buy a half-price ticket, say one more time, how old are you!" The ticket inspector was obviously particularly polite to her, hoping she would deny what she just said and change four years old to three years old.

But she didn't understand, she didn't understand the benefits of lying, she still answered that she was four years old. So she had to pay for a half-price ticket.

She is really foolish. In the south, there are too many smart people. Isn't this kind of problem something even a child knows how to deal with?

At dawn, the locomotive spewed white foam, like clouds, winding on the ground. It covered the desolate sandy plains, conjuring up beautiful landscapes in front of our eyes. I had walked this road ten years ago, but that was in the summer, the carriage windows were open, and all that came in was gray sand and dry heat. Now there are more and more trees on both sides, but unfortunately, they are all still bare. If it were spring, with the car windows closed, blocking the flying dust, and advancing in the green woods, I'm afraid you couldn't find such a beautiful journey anywhere else in China. (To be continued)

Last Testament (3) 209

— Lin Huiyin

It has been almost four months since Yina and Yijie left; at the time of leaving, she only felt a sense of abandonment, but now she is indeed under the pressure of life.

When Yijie had just left, she thought men were so ruthless, men who wanted to play everything, but in fact, before she could play a man, she was bound by a law. She thought that the reason why Yijie could leave her so easily was that there was no official status between her and him. She wanted a status first, if she were to be with any man again. If that law wasn't there, she could have cohabited with Yechu long ago. She felt she loved him, but she could never let go of his wife in his hometown.

And now what she feels most urgent is not how to get, or how to get a man, but how to solve the problem of her and her family's livelihood. If any acquaintance knew that what she needed to solve was such a problem, it would be laughable or unbelievable, this, she knew, but to herself, it was indeed a fact that could not be relaxed slightly, so she felt doubly sad. And the only key to why she didn't write much before but now always wants to write as long as someone asks her to write is the urgent need for稿費.

For the same reason, she agreed to write a novella for Xi Zhuoyun's Literary Bi-Weekly.

From the next day, that is, from Monday, Yina indeed began her "Taste of Life". She had warned her mother in advance to answer all phone calls to her saying "she is not at home," and locked herself in her small room day and night.

After about two weeks like this, "Taste of Life" was completed, with more than one hundred and forty manuscript papers. Completed, Yina was very happy and lighthearted. Because she thought that according to the pre-arranged four yuan per thousand words publication fee, she could get more than two hundred yuan, which could barely get her through the year. If she could sell the copyright at the same time, she could still be comfortable for a few days at the end of the year and the beginning of the year.

Although it is said that the end of the year is the beginning of the year, in fact, the new year had already passed at that time. The day she finished the manuscript was January 20, but it was the sixth day of the twelfth lunar month. - Yes, the end of the year she was talking about was the lunar new year, and only the lunar new year seemed to become a hurdle. Usually, she doesn't pay much attention to the lunar calendar, but as the end of the lunar year approaches, she almost completely forgets the solar calendar, she only remembers the lunar calendar. Especially this year, before the time had even entered December, she was worried about how to get through her new year. Therefore, now that she has finished writing her "Taste of Life", her joy and lightness are obviously not without reason.

The manuscript was finished in the evening, and the next day, the seventh day of the lunar month, was Sunday, and Xi Zhuoyun did not go to his office, and she was unwilling to go to his house, so she decided to postpone the submission of the manuscript to Monday.

And on Sunday, she invited one or two acquaintances, and had a good time playing for a day, to stretch her spirit and body that had been suppressed for two weeks.

Financial: US Bank Legislation Hopeless, Bullion Rises Another $8.70 210

—Central Bank Opens Current Account, Breaking $70 Mark—

The gold market was exceptionally strong yesterday due to the sudden shrinkage of silver prices, US banking leaders indicating no hope for silver legislation, and breaking through the $70 mark. In the morning, overseas silver markets in the UK and US fell in unison, with forward silver prices on the gold and silver exchange falling by 3.5 to 4.5 percent. Exchange rates fell slightly, London gold fell by two pence, US cotton fell by fourteen points, US wheat fell by 0.25, and stocks also fell by $1.65. The wool market opened and immediately rose to $64, but then due to a cable from the Associated Press stating that leaders of US banking groups had secretly reached an agreement with the President, indicating that there could be no further discussion of silver legislation in this session of Congress, and that the Fessinger-Vela and other cases were hopeless, the market rose even further. After opening, banks pooled together and rose, and later Reuters reported that a former US Treasury Secretary had strongly argued for the restoration of the international gold standard, and Professor Whalen also had a theory to restore the old monetary system, but at the same time, foreign telegrams stated that US banking group members would convene as early as April 2, without waiting for Rogers to return to the country. The gold market was extremely calm, hovering around $6. The Central Bank opened current accounts, and the situation remained stable, as did the exchange rate market. The underlying trend continued to rise. Later, the domestic banking market was unusually tight, and a telegram from Bombay reported a decline of ten annas. Public confidence was soaring, and the $70 mark was finally broken. March futures trading continued to rise, breaking through the $720 mark, one yuan higher than the closing price. Red gold was priced at $979, and boiled red gold was slightly weaker due to the influx of eastern goods. The swap discount was around one yuan. The Central Bank opened more than 300 current accounts at a price of $967, and it was heard that a small number were opened later at a price of $969.50. Specified Interbank Loan Rate Difficult to Implement Temporarily 213

The previous trial implementation of the prescribed foreign interbank loan rate, with a minimum of 5 points, unexpectedly resulted in an oversupply and a large disparity between supply and demand among the same industry in the morning, making it difficult to maintain the 5-point price. It was found that yesterday's check positions were as high as 1-2 million, and no one cared, so it was necessary to reduce the market price in order to sell off. As a result, the previous agreement was overturned, and the white loan market was reopened at 2 points. Therefore, the guild was in such a situation that it was difficult to force it, so it settled down and watched the movements. For the most part, there are still market prices of white loans and 2-3-4 points temporarily. If restrictions can be imposed in the future, it is necessary to wait for the opportunity to mature before determining the course of action.

Securities and Bond Markets Rise for Six Consecutive Days 215

1921 Customs Bonds Nearing 80%

Excessive Rise Requires Guarding Against Reversal

Yesterday, the rise in the Chinese Securities Exchange became more and more intense. The situation on the trading floor was extremely tense, and market prices soared, creating a "golden age" for government bond prices in spring. General psychology regarded it as a strange phenomenon. Since Friday of last week, after new high prices were discovered, this had been the sixth day, and no new high price had been discovered on any day. Observing the situation silently, at first there might be a small rebound, followed by a slight retreat at one point, but the rebound would inevitably exceed the retreat, and eventually the rise would become more and more vigorous, and new high prices would abound. Yesterday's situation, from beginning to end, every sector and every item was rising, and the rise was particularly strong after the afternoon opening. In such a high-price market situation, a sudden rise of half a yuan in one sector was almost crazy. Both the Unified Salt Tax Bureau had broken through 65%, 1921 Customs was nearing 80%, and 2021 both were nearing 70%. Since the September 18th Incident, such high prices had not been seen. Although it was due to the squeeze, there was no shortage of new bulls. The abnormal development to this point may come to an end, and a slight rebound is also expected, because sellers on the trading floor, such as numbers 38, 53, and 79, were selling very aggressively, and the northern gang was also actively selling, so the closing salt tax short was slightly tired. The number of bulls inside and outside the market was relatively high, and retail short covering was gradually satisfied, so it is necessary to guard against a reversal. As a result, market prices continued to rise by 2-3 cents to one yuan. The total number of transactions was approximately 18-19 million, which was omitted due to the late closing. Serious Labor Strikes Cause New York Stock Market to Fall 216

According to a Wall Street Journal report from Sin Fung Foreign Firm, yesterday's New York stock market saw a sharp drop in various stocks, ranging from several corners to six dollars. This was because the labor strike situation remained severe, and traders were deeply concerned that although the government intended to stop the auto industry strike, it might be unable to do so. Therefore, many sold off their holdings. Later, due to the strength of Canadian securities, the market stabilized at closing. Many traders are adopting a wait-and-see approach, awaiting the development of the exchange management case. The small exchange market was mixed, with prices fluctuating unpredictably. Bonds and U.S. government bonds were mixed and slightly lower. Also, a report from our New York agent stated that (securities) are facing unrest due to labor strike issues, but the market lacks pressure. (Wheat) trading is almost at a standstill, with no positive news; the harvest is not prosperous, the southwest is still experiencing drought, and farmers continue to appeal for relief. (Cotton) has very few new transactions due to the chaotic situation, and bulls continue to sell off. There is slight unease regarding the labor strikes, and the spot market is quiet with a tendency to loosen. The Punkhead Act will be transferred to the Senate for discussion. According to the common opinion of brokers, it is only advisable to buy when prices fall, and traders should be cautious before the situation clears up. Old Standard Yarn Suffers the Worst Decline in Yarn and Flower Market 217

Heavy Selling Pressure

Bulls Unable to Sustain Support Alone

The yarn market is weakening, and the decline is sharp. This situation is entirely due to the adverse environment. Therefore, even though a certain factory is trying its best to maintain prices, the slightest bit of bad news causes sellers to rush in like a tidal wave, making it impossible for bulls to hold up the market alone. At the same time, rumors in the market suggest that the factory's opinions are still divided, and there are ample delivery chips, with more than 8,000 bales already delivered to warehouses. In this situation, sellers are particularly keen, and with U.S. cotton prices falling, the decline in old standards is becoming increasingly severe.
