New Situation Brewing in Grain and Flour Futures Market 221

—Market Prices Show Significant Improvement—

Yesterday in the flour market, after the morning opening, market conditions for all months turned favorable. The quoted price of foreign wheat, Chicago, continued to decrease by about one corner, while Canada had no market. When the morning market opened, it was rumored that the Yingkou gang had spot flour transactions, which stirred up long-dormant sentiment. Factory chips for this month were mostly automatically withdrawn, and the factory did not intend to release most of the chips, so people were fearless and rushed to buy, and the market became brisk. When the afternoon market opened, due to excessive speculative buying and price increases, speculative customers were no longer active, and the market was once again shaken step by step. It is said that this situation is due to an agreement among factories not to release new chips, which is closely related to the previous government wheat situation. Therefore, bulls disregarded the environment and arbitrarily raised prices. Judging from this situation, there must be significant internal discrepancies. As a result, this month's prices surged by 3.25 cents, May prices rose by 4 cents, June prices rose by 4.25 cents, and July and August prices rose by 2.5 cents.

This Month's Wheat Futures See a Rise Due to Short Squeeze 222

Yesterday in the wheat futures market, after the morning and afternoon openings, the market conditions for all months showed a sharp increase in near-term prices and flat or soft conditions for distant-term prices. The quoted price of foreign wheat, Chicago, decreased by about one corner, while Canada remained unchanged. However, the opening price for this month in the morning saw a sharp increase, as bulls, said to be factories, intended to squeeze the shorts. Therefore, the opening price was gradually raised to 4.25 or 6 cents. In the afternoon, the market did not open. Distant months, being new goods, remained soft, but overall trading was brisk without special changes. As a result, this month's prices increased by 8 cents, August prices increased by a small 2 cents, and there were no other significant changes. The spot wheat market is trending stable and brisk, slightly better by 2 to 3 cents. Wuhe wheat opened at 3.57 yuan, substandard at 5.5 yuan, Tongzhou wheat at 3.58 yuan, and Yingzhou wheat at 3.54 yuan, totaling 4,000 bales, which were handled by Fuxin.

Market Prices

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Asking for Bread Instead of Cruisers 245

— Guang Han

The global economic panic is deepening, the number of unemployed is increasing, and the social situation in various countries is becoming increasingly unstable. The ruling class in general is well aware that this is an extremely dangerous situation. However, the world's nations have long been developing in a distorted way. This development is always contradictory, and there is still no way to reconcile it. On the one hand, they witness hundreds of thousands of workers in their own countries who have no food or clothing, sinking deeper into misery, without thinking of saving them. On the other hand, they take the large sums of money squeezed from the people and use them to manufacture deadly weapons. They seem to think that in order to solve the unemployment problem, it is necessary to maintain the power of capitalism first. Therefore, they use all the country's wealth to build warships and create airships, while telling those who have no means of making a living to go hungry for the time being. Can warships and airships really reverse the misfortune of the depression? Everyone knows that the production organizations of modern capitalist countries already have many defects. The biggest of these defects is that the means of production are entirely in the hands of a few people. Therefore, even if military force can truly promote the expansion of capitalism, its profits will only be monopolized by a few special classes, and it will still have no impact on the lives of the masses. Recently, unemployed workers in London, England, saw through this point and organized a hunger march to petition the government, saying: "We ask for bread, not cruisers!"

Indeed, only bread can solve the hunger of the unemployed, and cruisers can only increase their pain. Bread can feed people, but cruisers kill people. Yet, which country in the world today is not robbing the bread from the mouths of the hungry and frantically rushing to build cruisers?

Cotton Cheongsam 246

— Boer

"Sir, are you very cold?" One morning, it was still a deep autumn morning, when I was still teaching at a school, I wore a newly sewn cotton cheongsam to school to teach, and one of the students asked me this. I told her yes, and added an explanation that I was wearing it so early because I was not feeling well. The elementary school student didn't understand after all, and two days later when she saw me still wearing the cheongsam, she asked me again with concern, "Sir, is your illness still not cured?" The weather, against people's wishes, insisted on not blowing a cold wind those few days, causing people to pay attention to my cotton cheongsam all day long, and I couldn't help but answer, "Yes, the illness is still not cured!" Pitifully, a pure good intention, received my cold sentence, and still glaring at her with her eyes, scaring her to death, and walking away without daring to say a second word.

When I returned home in the evening, the room faced north, and I thought about taking off the cheongsam and putting on a single one, but it seemed very cold. After thinking for a while, I still unbuttoned it, sat on the bed, and covered my bare feet with a blanket. I thought this would at least prevent the back of the cheongsam from getting a lot of wrinkles. Every day I took care of it like this, but in the eyes of others, it was already very old and dirty.

Regardless of how old and dirty it was, it was after all my only cotton cheongsam. Apart from it, I couldn't find two summer gauze cheongsams to use as autumn lined cheongsams. Before sewing it, I had also considered it for a long time, wanting to sew it into a lined one, but I was afraid that after wearing it for a short time, the weather would turn cold again, and then I wouldn't be able to find money to make a second one; if it was cotton, I wouldn't have to worry when it was severely cold, although I would be ridiculed for a while at present, so my cotton cheongsam was sewn on a certain day four months ago.

Recalling the night before Christmas, a friend insisted on dragging me to dance, I was very happy, but when I thought of myself wearing a half-old cotton cheongsam, and imagined the ladies and wives in the dance hall, either exposing their arms or exposing their chests and backs, but I was wearing a thick cotton cheongsam, wouldn't that attract attention and secret laughter? Old friends were too enthusiastic, no matter how much I declined, the result was that she arranged me to sit well on the left side of the dance hall, the music motivated my excitement, several times I also squeezed into the crowd and slid back and forth on the floor, sliding so much that a lot of sweat flowed out, and later I ran into many acquaintances, who all happily came to ask me to dance for a while. After a few hours, it became very difficult for me to endure. It was really too hot, the sweat was flowing as if I had been basking in the hot sun for half a day. I was really afraid that a bad smell would emanate from my body, the smell of those ladies was fragrant, but me, ah, I dare not say it.

This time, I really regretted the plan to make a cotton cheongsam at the time. There was no way but to leave the heavily heated dance hall earlier. Walking out to the side of the road, the cold wind blew on my face again, and at this time I thought again, after all, a cotton cheongsam is better! It's a pity that I've worn it too dark, and my brother also said that the top of my collar has black oil stains and it's very unsightly, so I made up my mind to send it to the laundry, and they gave me a list of washing fees for eight corners. Three days later, I was standing outside the glass window in an outdated single garment, watching it being washed very well and clipped among many other people's clothes. I thought it was my only cotton cheongsam, and I hoped that I could take it back next week and it would still belong to me.

However, the spring chill is still piercing, how difficult will it be to endure next week!

I love my cotton cheongsam, it is always my treasure.

"The Person Contemplating Suicide" 247

— Zi

"Hey, friend, where are you going? This bus turns back at the New World amusement park."

"To the Bund... Alas—"

"It doesn't go to the Bund. Get off at the New World."

"Alas—it's over!"

Inside a packed Route One bus, in a corner at the back, sat a middle-aged man in a Western suit. His head was tilted back, his eyes rolled upwards, and he sighed, muttering "It's over!" The other passengers stared at him with surprised looks, and the ticket seller, noticing, squeezed through the crowd to question him in the Shanghainese dialect. When the bus reached the New World, the ticket seller insisted he get off, saying, "The bus is turning back to the depot." He ignored them, continuing to sigh, shake his head, bite his lip, and wipe his eyes with a square black handkerchief.

"Who are you looking for at the Bund?" the young, impatient ticket seller asked like a judge.

"Going to the XXX pier on the Bund," the answer was heavy, mumbled, and unclear.

"What?... Pier?..."

"Alas! What pier is it to you! Who has the mind to argue with you? Alas!" This time the sigh was sharp, and his voice trembled slightly.

"A suicidal person!" the passengers whispered, convinced of his strange behavior.

The bus stopped at the Bund station. I nodded to my companion and followed the strange man out of the bus and into the crowd. He staggered south, oblivious to the oncoming cars, seemingly rushing towards the river. Intrigued by his odd behavior, and worried he might actually be suicidal, I rushed forward and grabbed his arm.

"Hey, why are you running towards the river like you're trying to die?" I asked, breathless.

"..." He looked at me, his eyes showing gratitude for my concern.

"Are you trying to kill yourself?" I asked again, loudly.

"No... Why do you people say such awful things, asking someone if they want to kill themselves?"

"Then why are you running to the river? Friend, I have some free time today. Let's talk." I took his arm and walked west along Avenue Edward VII. I learned that he was from Taiyuan, Shanxi, studied mechanical engineering in France for five years, returned to China in 1932, and was now a French secretary for the Kunming municipal government in Yunnan. He was heading home because his beloved wife had died, and his father had wired him to return for the funeral.

"Have you been to Shanghai before? Do you have any companions? Where are you staying?"

"I'm alone. This is my first time in Shanghai... Alas..."

"If you have something troubling you, we are all brothers. Tell me, and we can think of a solution together. Have you had dinner yet?"

"Alas! I'm penniless and at my wit's end. I've been in Shanghai for two days and only had one bowl of noodles. I only have forty cents left. What dinner can I have! I've slept with ghosts for two nights! Alas..."

"Friend, let me treat you to dinner. Can you translate French? I can recommend you for a job!"

"Alas, why are you so annoying, dragging me along? Let me go. I have things to do. I don't need your help." He broke free of my grip and turned to walk east again. I had intended to help him find work, but he was blaming me. I was annoyed, but I was also beginning to suspect him. I grabbed his arm again and walked west, then north, then west, then north again, and then west again. On the way, I asked him about some friends who had recently returned from studying in France. When I mentioned their names, he always repeated them, saying they sounded familiar, but he couldn't recall their situations. Later, I asked him about a Mr. Zhu who had studied mechanical engineering in France at the same time as him and had recently become mentally ill due to unemployment. He replied that there was no such person who studied mechanical engineering in France.

"Hey, you have nothing better to do, but don't delay me. Are you dragging me along to kidnap me? Let go!" As we walked calmly towards a tall red-walled building, he struggled desperately to break free, pulling backwards. I said gently, "Why? Friend, China needs talent! Mechanical engineers will have their day... Let's go eat dinner..."

"Don't joke around. If you're treating me to dinner, why are you dragging me here? Why didn't we eat at the restaurant we just passed?" Ah, we had already walked onto the quietest part of the Fourth Avenue. Wasn't the building ahead the police station? Oh, the police station. His earlier "Don't joke around... why are we coming here?..." rang clearly in my mind. I realized everything. I thought clearly, "Let's test him." I said sternly,

"Look, I'm a detective from the police station. Come with me to the station for a while." I showed him the badge on my inner shirt but quickly put my shirt back down.

"Friend, why are we joking with each other? Let's go our separate ways." He angrily shook off my hand and strode south.

Women's Professions 248

— Shen Min

The topic of women's professions can be said to be an important issue in society today. However, the author is not female, and is not particularly close to women. Furthermore, the issue is too complex to be fully examined in a short piece. Therefore, I only intend to contribute some personal observations on certain aspects of the issue.

Everything has a cause. The cause of the women's profession issue can be traced back to the history of women's liberation. Traditionally, women were confined to the home, with no place outside it. Their lives were too restricted, so they sought liberation. The initial stage of this liberation was women seeking education. If we recall the past few years, most educated female compatriots were fighting for the opportunity to study. Later, this issue was resolved due to the momentum of the times, although not without some setbacks. However, education is only a prelude to liberation. In other words, education only provides some knowledge and technical skills. With knowledge and skills, there is a natural desire to use them. Furthermore, the entire issue of women's liberation cannot be considered complete with mere education. Therefore, the issue of women's professions is the second step in women's liberation, and the most important issue today.

The tide of the times is fierce. Every breaking wave has many victims. This is a reality we are told. The women's profession issue is like such a wave, currently unfolding. Thus, when we open the daily newspapers, we see many reports of victims in this tide. At the same time, in this economically depressed society, finding a career for women seems exceedingly difficult.

Therefore, when studying this issue, we must consider women's safety. Some may say that this is a problem of the entire social organization and must be addressed through social reform. I think that might not be entirely true. In my opinion, women themselves must solve it. My contribution is this: unmarried women should fully prepare themselves with various practical skills and knowledge. When they find a partner, they can help their husbands in their work. For example, if the husband is a doctor, then the wife can be his assistant or a nurse. If the husband is a merchant, then the wife can do accounting. For married women, it is even easier. They only need to do what they can within their husband's field of work. In this way, women will face fewer inconveniences and dangers outside of work. Furthermore, husbands will be more motivated in their careers with a loyal and reliable assistant. At the same time, many obstacles in the women's profession issue can be avoided.

Some may say that my proposal still implies that "women are appendages to men." This statement seems reasonable on the surface, but in reality, it is a non-issue. Because in today's society, except for a very small minority, whether men or women working outside the home, are afraid of not being oppressed? Rather than being someone else's appendage, it is better to be one's husband's appendage. Furthermore, when women work under their husbands, they are nominally helping their husbands, but in reality, they are cooperating with each other. On the other hand, they also monitor each other's actions. As a result, they can certainly trust and be happy with each other. At the same time, it can be said to be the true essence of gender equality; the goal of women's liberation!

However, I wrote this article specifically for women in intellectual circles. I will include this as a postscript to conclude this article!

Ding Yuanwai of Dingjia Village, Huzhou, relied on his power and wealth. He privately created a fish tax, forcing fishermen to pay him—he would sit and collect a lot of money, and would not allow any to be owed. This drawing shows fishermen respectfully paying the fish tax.

Spring Evening Wedding Banquet 252

— You Qi

It was early spring weather, the chill was gone from the air, containing a gentle breeze, blowing on people's bodies, refreshing.

Ah, how precious, this spring evening's undulation.

Carrying pent-up depression, treading on the magnificent Nanjing Road, BulckFordDonge... glossy and smooth, rolling by, like a gust of wind, passed the outbuilding.

"Let's sit for a while, huh?" "Let's go!"

Outside the window of the Wing On Company building, such a sentence flew out, an oriole's voice, the sound waves, so harmonious and delicate!

Stepping on the stone steps of the Da Dong Restaurant, my heart fluttered!

"They won't kick me out, will they? Maybe, they will question me in detail—like treating me as a thief?" I pondered, unable to restrain myself.

Fortunately, the busy them, did not seem to notice me. So, quietly, along the thick felt, I stepped upstairs, the sound was very low.

Bright electric lights, suspended at a passageway entrance, under the lights stood many people wearing neat white shirts, very dignified. Their eyes were fixed on me, as if searching for something, at this, I trembled, almost losing the courage to move forward.

Thank heaven, I finally escaped that difficult pass, although it went through a degree of interrogation.

Entering the hall, what flashed before my eyes were: white tablecloths, white chair covers, countless heads, bodies of varying heights, red silk draperies, yellow gold characters... all this, teasing me, I felt as if countless sparks were jumping around in front of me.

Finally, I was also placed on a white upholstered chair. After a considerable period of time, I felt that the eyes of these people were not as sharp as those outside the passageway, at this, the previous courage slowly recovered.

The roof, snow-white, in each square compartment, milky light bulbs were emitting milky light, one by one, dissolving on people's faces, revealing the vitality of spring.

At the southern end, on the platform with the double happiness characters made of red neon tubes, the halo, red, soaked the fresh flowers, look, she was smiling.

Hair fragrance, powder fragrance, skin fragrance, all kinds of fragrant mist were broadcast by fashionable female guests, blowing on the hearts of young people, blowing on the nostrils of old people; fawn, ochre, coffee, dark black... different colors, covering different graceful figures.

Melon seeds, being peeled in everyone's mouth, the shells were casually spit on the ground, cigarettes, being smoked at will, the smoke lightly lingering in the room: bananas, the peels peeled off, "thump"! The tip with the black spot, was spat by delicate red lips onto a clean plate.

The dishes, were being changed, one by one, the wine, in large copper pots, poured into small silver pots, then sent into people's stomachs. After the bride and groom revealed smiles and "toured to toast", a scene of chaos! Gradually thinned and quieted down.

Leaving the door of Da Dong, the wind, blowing in my face, gentle, blowing on people's bodies, the chill was gone from the air, it was early spring weather.

Ah! How precious, this spring evening's undulation.

Novel

Rain (4) 254

— Zhang Yiping

The rain beat vigorously on the roof, showing no signs of stopping. Yuan Wen glanced at the window, misted over with water vapor, and said to himself,

"I should go back..."

"So early."

As soon as he finished speaking, the tea server poked his head in and asked, "Mr. Zhu, are you eating dinner?" Before I could answer, Sister Wen interjected, "Then I'll go back! Do you have an umbrella to borrow?"

As she asked the tea server about an umbrella, I said to her, "Eat dinner first, or wait for the rain to stop. It's not convenient walking alone in the rain. You can't get a taxi at this time."

"Then you can take me!" she said directly and cheerfully.

I hesitated.

"You don't have to," she said, smiling.

I nodded and said, "I'll take you." I turned around and told the tea server that I wouldn't be eating, and asked them to eat first.

Stepping outside, I saw endless rain. The lights on Ge Ling were vaguely visible, flickering uncertainly in the rain. The two of us shared an umbrella and walked slowly along the Su Causeway, not speaking. The sound of our footsteps, mixed with the sound of the rain, created a unique scene. I had been in Hangzhou for almost half a year and often liked to wander around on my own. I thought I had seen all the scenic spots in Hangzhou, but the West Lake after the rain had a different kind of beauty. This thought flashed through my mind, and I wanted to send her back to school early so I could enjoy the rain alone, so I quickened my pace.

"Walk slower." Her right arm bumped the hand holding the umbrella. "Are you afraid of ghosts on the way back?" She laughed uncontrollably. The umbrella tilted in the wind, splashing her face with rain.

After walking the length of the Su Causeway, we turned left, and we were at her school. She knocked on the door and said to me, "My colleagues at school are good to me, but I can't get along with them. I often force myself to agree with them, which is too boring. Come talk to me when you have time. It's been more than two years since we last met."

I nodded casually, and hurried back. As soon as I stepped onto the Su Causeway, two people rushed ahead from behind. They had no rain gear, and they were soaked. The shorter one carried a basket containing several bowls of food, which could no longer be distinguished as fish or meat, as well as incense burners and candle holders for offerings. The taller one was panting. He looked like he had lost his balance while running, swaying from side to side. The shorter one said, "Mom, be careful!" Only then did I realize that they were a mother and son returning from sweeping the tombs.

Filled with the anticipation of enjoying the rain, I saw them mother and son, and suddenly changed my mind. Pointlessly going, and my cousin would resent me for being too cold, what have the peach blossoms changed in the corner of the school gate, and at the same time thinking the colleagues thought I was a mysterious guest? And then without thinking, I began reciting the phrase "During the Qingming festival, the rain falls in torrents, travelers on the road are dejected!" (End)

Movie Special

Black Drama Masterpiece "The Emperor Jones" Now Made into Film 255

— Chen Xiong

Black people seem to be given us special recognition in our money-worshipping cities, especially in trendy dance halls. Every night, performance programs often include black people dancing, black people doing comedy, and black people performing acrobatic stunts. It seems that besides entertaining people, black people don't have to do anything else.

We know that several famous works of American literature are about the lives of black people. The most famous author is Harriet Beecher Stowe, whose book "Uncle Tom's Cabin," translated by Lin Qin Nan in our country, was made into a film called "Black Slave's Soul" by Universal Pictures. A few years ago, the famous director King Vidor made a black religious film called "Hallelujah," which was also a masterpiece that caused a sensation in the film industry.

The black drama "The Emperor Jones" by Eugene O'Neill, translated by Hong Shen and Gu Zhongyi, was made into a film by United Artists last year and will be shown in the local area soon. The film's translation has been changed to "The Fall of the Overlord." The original play is a one-act drama divided into eight scenes. The stage performance begins with the character Jones as the emperor of a small island. At this time, his final days are approaching. The islanders are rebelling, and the remaining seven scenes describe Jones frantically running for his life in the forest. The film "The Emperor Jones" recounts the facts before Jones became emperor, which seems to be more detailed than the stage play. The second half of the film, which depicts Jones as emperor, is very similar to the stage play.

Previous O'Neill dramas made into films include "Anna Christie" starring Greta Garbo (translated as "Blue Water Love") and "Strange Interlude" starring Norma Shearer (translated as "Red Powder Drifting"). When the stage play "Strange Interlude" was performed in New York, it opened at 2 pm and did not end until 11 pm. In between, there were meal and rest times for the audience. This could be considered a strange interlude. The play "The Emperor Jones" has had three different performances: the first is the stage play, with the famous actor Charles Gilpin playing Jones; the second is the opera, with the singing star Lawrence Tibbett, who once made a splash on the silver screen with Lu Fanli in "Eternal Regret", playing Jones; and the third is the film drama.

Paul Robeson, the actor who plays the main character in the film "The Emperor Jones", is more famous than Charles Gilpin in the stage play and Lawrence Tibbett in the opera. This is because Robeson has played Jones in all three different performances of "The Emperor Jones" – stage, opera, and film. Robeson is originally black, so his portrayal of Jones is even more realistic and thorough. Robeson graduated from Columbia University Law School in the United States, but he did not become a lawyer and instead became an actor. He also has a natural singing voice that is well-suited for opera. His first stage appearance was in O'Neill's "All God's Chillun Got Wings," followed by "The Emperor Jones." A few years ago, Robeson performed the song and dance of "The Emperor Jones" in London, which was greatly welcomed by the King and Queen of England.

Because Robeson is a black person, but he is also a scholar, and the British do not discriminate against black people like the Americans do, so in England, writers H.G. Wells, Prime Minister Ramsay MacDonald, former Prime Minister David Lloyd George, and the Prince of Wales all treated him as a guest. Because Robeson was treated so generously by the British, he did not want to return to the United States. But United Artists hired him to star in the film "The Emperor Jones," so after the film was made, he went to England to live permanently.

Film Review

Review of "People Behind the Scenes" 256

— Ling He

—Central—

When we review Chinese literary works, there are many excellent creations that show that the Chinese literary scene has indeed achieved encouraging results. But at the same time, there are indeed too many shoddy things. This is not only due to generally empty and shallow content, but also to the extremely backwardness in creative skills. Naturally, this is a very terrible phenomenon.

Similarly, it is even more so in the field of film. On the one hand, there are relatively excellent works such as "Life" and "The Wrath of the China Sea," and on the other hand, there are films like "People Behind the Scenes." Hasn't "Sister Flowers" been showing for more than thirty days and trying to break "Eskimo's" world box office record? Although the film itself does have many unsatisfactory aspects, it has already greatly surprised European and American film merchants. However, our filmmakers should consider how to further promote this glory? This is something the creators of "People Behind the Scenes" should pay attention to.

"People Behind the Scenes" is a product of Yue Ming Company. We will not forget the same company's "Bad Neighbors," although that was also a childish thing, it was much better than "People Behind the Scenes."

In any case, "People Behind the Scenes" is a work below the baseline. The reason is to desperately cater to the audience's low-level interests, so regardless, love, martial arts, detective, ethics, all kinds of things are forced together in an ugly way.

Some people say that we should be more lenient towards the productions of small companies, and we cannot use the same standards as large companies. Whether this statement is appropriate, I do not want to say more here, but, like the boring stuff of "People Behind the Scenes," if we do not also give it strict criticism, isn't that intentionally ruining the future of Chinese cinema?

I hope that the creators of "People Behind the Scenes" will no longer treat film as child's play, and will humbly put in a lot of hard work in research, otherwise I am afraid that they will be abandoned by the progressive audience forever.

Review of "Lucky Girl" 257

— Highland

“MaidHappy”—Guanglu Lanxin—

When a film's author is creating it, if for the sake of convenience in their script, they freely develop the story, and in terms of screenwriting, directing, etc., they only seek simplicity and speed, using fragmented images from real life to complete their story, without considering whether this fragmented image is appropriate or realistic in the play or scene, it is easy for the playwright, but in terms of the value of the work, it becomes a big problem.

All great works of art are nothing more than a true expression of life. Lacking authenticity, there is no artistic value. The creative attitude towards artistic works needs to be serious. The reason why great works of art are produced is arduous work, and it is for this reason.

In "Lucky Girl", the author uses fragmented images from life to complete their story, without considering the authenticity of life.

The most important thing, for example: a young and handsome diplomat gives a top-secret diplomatic card to a young girl, forming the center of this drama. Many characters are active around this event. In real life, we find it difficult to see this kind of fact. It can be said that it is

The Beginning of Love Fire—Gao Zhanfei and Tan Ying's Expressions in Lianhua's Epic Film "Wind", Directed by Wu Cun 258

extremely exceptional. There are many coincidences in the rest of the plot. Many important keys and turning points are very fictional. What we see is not life, but a fake play, just to have these opportunities for the actors to meet, talk, sing, pile up some facts, and end with a final kiss.

Britain is an old empire. The development of all industries and cultures was very early. They maintained the lives of their upper class by exploiting colonies and domestic farmers and workers. Therefore, what the upper class needed was only light-hearted humor and leisurely music to satisfy their feelings after exploitation. They are unwilling to touch real life, and even if they do, they distort it. It is also reasonable that it is difficult for valuable works to appear in British films (of course, other films are rarely exceptions).

It is difficult for a director to unfold his skills in such a story, and Mansfieldmarkbam, in addition to putting considerable effort into the musical effects, is as clumsy as the screenwriter in other aspects.

Charlotteand and JohannesRiemann did not have enough room to develop their skills in such a story. Charlotteander's performance skills are not as good as J. Riemann. In addition, the old male and female professors and the swindlers can express the unique character of that kind of person, and they get some fragmented effects from their characters, which of course are laughable effects. The background is in Switzerland, and the scenery seen on the scene, the life in the night garden, these places can be regarded as fulfilling the task of "introducing the scenery". If it is purely to introduce the scenery of Switzerland, as a documentary film, the meaning may be better.

Film Novel

Catherine the Great ScarletEmpress (13) 261

— Sumei

In that large hall, in the stillness of the night, suddenly a black shadow was moving. The bright moonlight of winter shone in through the window, reflecting on the floor and walls, transforming into terrifying black and white shadows. The black shadow moved step by step, step by step, and soon passed the guard post and disappeared into Catherine's bedroom.

"Be careful," Captain Woronov bent down and told the queen sleeping in bed. "Everything is ready, Your Majesty, please hurry." Catherine climbed out of bed. She was wearing a guard's uniform, and said in her mouth, "I'm ready... why did I wait so impatiently that I fell asleep." As she spoke, she followed Woronov out of the bedroom and ran into the large hall. A guard came to challenge her, but Woronov was quick and tied him up in one fell swoop. In this way, they quickly left the palace. Catherine ran to the barracks. The soldiers recognized her as the queen and immediately swore to sacrifice their lives for her and annihilate her enemies. Everyone shouted slogans: "Long live Catherine! Death to the Tsar!" In this way, they set off in formation, with Catherine leading the way on a white horse. At the same time, in the church, all the priests were also holding a meeting. When Catherine arrived, they all unanimously supported her as the head of the church. The priests all ran to kiss her hands and feet. A priest asked, "Can we ring the bell? All of Russia is waiting for this bell." Catherine went to ring the big bell herself without saying a word.

Peter was in the palace, and when he heard the bell, he jumped up. He left the bedroom and walked into the corridor, where he saw his guard tied up and lying on the ground. He shouted, "Why is the bell ringing? What does this mean?" A person in the black shadow replied, "Peter, you will naturally understand soon." Captain Woronov walked out freely. As soon as Peter saw him, he shouted, "Do you still want your head? Don't you know I'm the emperor?" Woronov said, "The emperor is gone. Now there is only the queen." After he finished speaking, he pulled a napkin out of his mouth. Peter knew that something was wrong, and while shouting for help, he wanted to escape into the bedroom, but Woronov took a step forward, and something was already around his neck. He immediately knelt down, a wave of darkness in front of him, and he had lost consciousness. Woronov ran to Peter's bedroom and saw that Elizabeth was pale with fright and trembling. Woronov said, "Are you still not running away? Are you still waiting for the queen's soldiers to come and tear you to pieces?" As he spoke, he came out.

That day was the day of Catherine's coronation ceremony. It is known that the coronation ceremony was held in the auditorium. The priests chanted praises. A high priest sang: "Our sorrows have come to an end, our happiness is about to begin... Your sincere love for Russia has spread far and wide, so all the people of Russia deeply hope that you will ascend the throne early, remove their shackles, and abolish all previous dangerous policies... Now God and his angels will remain with us forever... May your enemies tremble in the dust... Few of those who wear this crown have been glorious monarchs, but may you further enhance its splendor and fame." After speaking, he placed the brilliant crown on Catherine's head. The priests and ministers all ran forward to kiss her hand. The haggard and pale Alexey was also mixed in with the crowd, shrinking back and daring not to step forward. Catherine saw it and smiled to herself, "Who can predict the things of the world?" (End)
